<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Pneumonia</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Pneumonia_(disambiguation)" title="Pneumonia (disambiguation)">Pneumonia (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_edema" title="Pulmonary edema">pulmonary edema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_embolism" title="Pulmonary embolism">pulmonary embolism</a><sup class="reference" therapy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011Tx_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011Tx-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Frequency</th><td class="infobox-data">450 million (7%) per year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CochraneTx13_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-CochraneTx13-13">[13]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Deaths</th><td class="infobox-data">Four million per year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CochraneTx13_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-CochraneTx13-13">[13]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Pneumonia</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammatory</a> condition of the <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">lung</a> primarily affecting the small air sacs known as <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_alveolus" title="Pulmonary alveolus">alveoli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RespText09_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-RespText09-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AcuteCare09_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-AcuteCare09-14">[14]</a></sup> Symptoms typically include some combination of <a href="/wiki/Phlegm" title="Phlegm">productive</a> or dry <a href="/wiki/Cough" title="Cough">cough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chest_pain" title="Chest pain">chest pain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fever" title="Fever">fever</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shortness_of_breath" title="Shortness of breath">difficulty breathing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ash2007_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ash2007-15">[15]</a></sup> The severity of the condition is variable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ash2007_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ash2007-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Pneumonia is usually caused by <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a> with <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>, and less commonly by other <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[a]</a></sup> Identifying the responsible pathogen can be difficult. Diagnosis is often based on symptoms and <a href="/wiki/Physical_examination" title="Physical examination">physical examination</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011Diag_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011Diag-8">[8]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest_X-ray" title="Chest X-ray">Chest X-rays</a>, blood tests, and <a href="/wiki/Microbiological_culture" title="Microbiological culture">culture</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sputum" title="Sputum">sputum</a> may help confirm the diagnosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011Diag_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011Diag-8">[8]</a></sup> The disease may be classified by where it was acquired, such as community- or hospital-acquired or healthcare-associated pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Risk factors for pneumonia include <a href="/wiki/Cystic_fibrosis" title="Cystic fibrosis">cystic fibrosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">chronic obstructive pulmonary disease</a> (COPD), <a href="/wiki/Sickle_cell_disease" title="Sickle cell disease">sickle cell disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes">diabetes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heart_failure" title="Heart failure">heart failure</a>, a history of <a href="/wiki/Smoking" title="Smoking">smoking</a>, a poor ability to cough (such as following a <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a>), and a <a href="/wiki/Immunosuppression" title="Immunosuppression">weak immune system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2022_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2022-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2020SCD_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2020SCD-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vaccine" title="Vaccine">Vaccines</a> to prevent certain types of pneumonia (such as those caused by <i><a href="/wiki/Streptococcus_pneumoniae" title="Streptococcus pneumoniae">Streptococcus pneumoniae</a></i> bacteria, linked to <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a>, or linked to <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a>) are available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011Pre_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011Pre-10">[10]</a></sup> Other methods of prevention include <a href="/wiki/Hand_washing" title="Hand washing">hand washing</a> to prevent infection, not smoking, and social distancing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011Pre_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011Pre-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Treatment depends on the underlying cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011-20">[19]</a></sup> Pneumonia believed to be due to bacteria is treated with <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">antibiotics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011Tx_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011Tx-11">[11]</a></sup> If the pneumonia is severe, the affected person is generally hospitalized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011-20">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_therapy" title="Oxygen therapy">Oxygen therapy</a> may be used if oxygen levels are low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2011Tx_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2011Tx-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Each year, pneumonia affects about 450 million people globally (7% of the population) and results in about 4 million deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CochraneTx13_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-CochraneTx13-13">[13]</a></sup> With the introduction of antibiotics and vaccines in the 20th century, survival has greatly improved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup> Nevertheless, pneumonia remains a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leading_cause_of_death" title="Leading cause of death">leading cause of death</a> in developing countries, and also among the very old, the very young, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chronic_(medicine)" title="Chronic (medicine)">chronically</a> ill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-5"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> Pneumonia often shortens the period of suffering among those already close to death and has thus been called "the old man's friend".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBMED05_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED05-22">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="247" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Pneumonia.webm" height="174" id="mwe_player_2" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Pneumonia.webm/310px-seek%3D20-En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Pneumonia.webm.jpg" preload="none" width="310"><source data-bandwidth="339160" data-framerate="25" data-height="720" data-shorttitle="WebM source" data-title="Original WebM file, 1,280 × 720 (339 kbps)" data-width="1280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d5/En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Pneumonia.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><track data-dir="ltr" kind="subtitles" label="English ‪(en)‬" src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AEn.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Pneumonia.webm&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" srclang="en" type="text/vtt"/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Pneumonia.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Video summary (<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:VideoWiki/Pneumonia" title="Wikipedia:VideoWiki/Pneumonia">script</a>)</div></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Signs_and_symptoms">Signs and symptoms</span></h2>
<table align="right" class="wikitable" style="margin-left:0.4em;">
<tbody><tr>
<th colspan="2">Symptoms frequency<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint10_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tint10-23">[22]</a></sup>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th>Symptom</th>
<th>Frequency
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>Cough</td>
<td style="text-align: center;">79–91%
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Fatigue</td>
<td style="text-align: center;">90%
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Fever</td>
<td style="text-align: center;">71–75%
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Shortness of breath</td>
<td style="text-align: center;">67–75%
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Sputum</td>
<td style="text-align: center;">60–65%
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Chest pain</td>
<td style="text-align: center;">39–49%
</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Symptoms_of_pneumonia.svg"><img alt="A diagram of the human body outlining the key symptoms of pneumonia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1045" data-file-width="1055" decoding="async" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Symptoms_of_pneumonia.svg/290px-Symptoms_of_pneumonia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Symptoms_of_pneumonia.svg/435px-Symptoms_of_pneumonia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Symptoms_of_pneumonia.svg/580px-Symptoms_of_pneumonia.svg.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Symptoms_of_pneumonia.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main symptoms of infectious pneumonia</div></div></div>
<p>People with infectious pneumonia often have a <a href="/wiki/Cough" title="Cough">productive cough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fever" title="Fever">fever</a> accompanied by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rigors" title="Rigors">shaking chills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shortness_of_breath" title="Shortness of breath">shortness of breath</a>, sharp or stabbing <a href="/wiki/Chest_pain" title="Chest pain">chest pain</a> during deep breaths, and an increased <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_rate" title="Respiratory rate">rate of breathing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ06_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ06-9">[9]</a></sup> In elderly people, confusion may be the most prominent sign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ06_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ06-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>The typical signs and symptoms in children under five are fever, cough, and fast or difficult breathing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Develop11_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Develop11-24">[23]</a></sup> Fever is not very specific, as it occurs in many other common illnesses and may be absent in those with severe disease, <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> or in the elderly. In addition, a cough is frequently absent in children less than 2 months old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Develop11_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Develop11-24">[23]</a></sup> More severe signs and symptoms in children may include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_cyanosis" title="Central cyanosis">blue-tinged skin</a>, unwillingness to drink, convulsions, ongoing vomiting, extremes of temperature, or a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decreased_level_of_consciousness" title="Decreased level of consciousness">decreased level of consciousness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Develop11_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Develop11-24">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bacterial and viral cases of pneumonia usually result in similar symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOPrevent2012_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHOPrevent2012-26">[25]</a></sup> Some causes are associated with classic, but non-specific, clinical characteristics. Pneumonia caused by <i><a href="/wiki/Legionella" title="Legionella">Legionella</a></i> may occur with abdominal pain, <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrhea</a>, or confusion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> Pneumonia caused by <i><a href="/wiki/Streptococcus_pneumoniae" title="Streptococcus pneumoniae">Streptococcus pneumoniae</a></i> is associated with rusty colored sputum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Pneumonia caused by <i><a href="/wiki/Klebsiella" title="Klebsiella">Klebsiella</a></i> may have bloody sputum often described as "currant jelly".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint10_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tint10-23">[22]</a></sup> Bloody sputum (known as <a href="/wiki/Hemoptysis" title="Hemoptysis">hemoptysis</a>) may also occur with <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>, Gram-negative pneumonia, <a href="/wiki/Lung_abscess" title="Lung abscess">lung abscesses</a> and more commonly <a href="/wiki/Acute_bronchitis" title="Acute bronchitis">acute bronchitis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> Pneumonia caused by <i><a href="/wiki/Mycoplasma_pneumoniae" title="Mycoplasma pneumoniae">Mycoplasma pneumoniae</a></i> may occur in association with <a href="/wiki/Cervical_lymphadenopathy" title="Cervical lymphadenopathy">swelling of the lymph nodes in the neck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthralgia" title="Arthralgia">joint pain</a>, or a <a href="/wiki/Otitis_media" title="Otitis media">middle ear infection</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> Viral pneumonia presents more commonly with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wheezing" title="Wheezing">wheezing</a> than bacterial pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOPrevent2012_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHOPrevent2012-26">[25]</a></sup> Pneumonia was historically divided into "typical" and "atypical" based on the belief that the presentation predicted the underlying cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M32_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-M32-29">[28]</a></sup> However, evidence has not supported this distinction, therefore it is no longer emphasized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M32_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-M32-29">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cause">Cause</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Streptococcus_pneumoniae.jpg"><img alt="Three lone round objects in a black background" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Streptococcus_pneumoniae.jpg/220px-Streptococcus_pneumoniae.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Streptococcus_pneumoniae.jpg/330px-Streptococcus_pneumoniae.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Streptococcus_pneumoniae.jpg/440px-Streptococcus_pneumoniae.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Streptococcus_pneumoniae.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The bacterium <i><a href="/wiki/Streptococcus_pneumoniae" title="Streptococcus pneumoniae">Streptococcus pneumoniae</a></i>, a common cause of pneumonia, imaged by an <a href="/wiki/Electron_microscope" title="Electron microscope">electron microscope</a></div></div></div>
<p>Pneumonia is due to infections caused primarily by <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> or <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a> and less commonly by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungi" title="Fungi">fungi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasites" title="Parasites">parasites</a>. Although more than 100 strains of infectious agents have been identified, only a few are responsible for the majority of cases. Mixed infections with both viruses and bacteria may occur in roughly 45% of infections in children and 15% of infections in adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-6"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup> A causative agent may not be isolated in about half of cases despite careful testing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBMED05_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED05-22">[21]</a></sup> In an active population-based surveillance for community-acquired pneumonia requiring hospitalization in five hospitals in Chicago and Nashville from January 2010 through June 2012, 2259 patients were identified who had radiographic evidence of pneumonia and specimens that could be tested for the responsible pathogen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPIC2015_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPIC2015-30">[29]</a></sup> Most patients (62%) had no detectable pathogens in their sample, and unexpectedly, respiratory viruses were detected more frequently than bacteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPIC2015_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPIC2015-30">[29]</a></sup> Specifically, 23% had one or more viruses, 11% had one or more bacteria, 3% had both bacterial and viral pathogens, and 1% had a fungal or mycobacterial infection. "The most common pathogens were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_rhinovirus" title="Human rhinovirus">human rhinovirus</a> (in 9% of patients), influenza virus (in 6%), and <i>Streptococcus pneumoniae</i> (in 5%)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPIC2015_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-EPIC2015-30">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term <i>pneumonia</i> is sometimes more broadly applied to any condition resulting in <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammation</a> of the lungs (caused for example by <a href="/wiki/Autoimmune_disease" title="Autoimmune disease">autoimmune diseases</a>, chemical burns or drug reactions); however, this inflammation is more accurately referred to as <a href="/wiki/Pneumonitis" title="Pneumonitis">pneumonitis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isbn0-7234-3200-7_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-isbn0-7234-3200-7-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowden2010_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bowden2010-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>Factors that predispose to pneumonia include <a href="/wiki/Smoking" title="Smoking">smoking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immunodeficiency" title="Immunodeficiency">immunodeficiency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">alcoholism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">chronic obstructive pulmonary disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sickle_cell_disease" title="Sickle cell disease">sickle cell disease</a> (SCD), <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chronic_kidney_disease" title="Chronic kidney disease">chronic kidney disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liver_disease" title="Liver disease">liver disease</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_aging" title="Biological aging">biological aging</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2020SCD_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2020SCD-7">[7]</a></sup> Additional risks in children include not being <a href="/wiki/Breastfeeding" title="Breastfeeding">breastfed</a>, exposure to cigarette smoke and other air pollution, <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>, and poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> The use of acid-suppressing medications – such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proton-pump_inhibitors" title="Proton-pump inhibitors">proton-pump inhibitors</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H2_blockers" title="H2 blockers">H2 blockers</a> – is associated with an increased risk of pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> Approximately 10% of people who require <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_ventilation" title="Mechanical ventilation">mechanical ventilation</a> develop <a href="/wiki/Ventilator-associated_pneumonia" title="Ventilator-associated pneumonia">ventilator-associated pneumonia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ar2016_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ar2016-34">[33]</a></sup> and people with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gastric_feeding_tube" title="Gastric feeding tube">gastric feeding tube</a> have an increased risk of developing <a href="/wiki/Aspiration_pneumonia" title="Aspiration pneumonia">aspiration pneumonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> For people with certain variants of the <a href="/wiki/FER_(gene)" title="FER (gene)">FER gene</a>, the risk of death is reduced in <a href="/wiki/Sepsis" title="Sepsis">sepsis</a> caused by pneumonia. However, for those with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TLR6" title="TLR6">TLR6</a> variants, the risk of getting <a href="/wiki/Legionnaires%27_disease" title="Legionnaires' disease">Legionnaires' disease</a> is increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elena_2015_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elena_2015-36">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bacteria">Bacteria</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bacterial_pneumonia" title="Bacterial pneumonia">Bacterial pneumonia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MRSAPneumoCT.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="734" data-file-width="879" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/MRSAPneumoCT.png/220px-MRSAPneumoCT.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/MRSAPneumoCT.png/330px-MRSAPneumoCT.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/MRSAPneumoCT.png/440px-MRSAPneumoCT.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MRSAPneumoCT.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cavitating pneumonia due to MRSA as seen on a CT scan</div></div></div>
<p>Bacteria are the most common cause of <a href="/wiki/Community-acquired_pneumonia" title="Community-acquired pneumonia">community-acquired pneumonia</a> (CAP), with <i><a href="/wiki/Streptococcus_pneumoniae" title="Streptococcus pneumoniae">Streptococcus pneumoniae</a></i> isolated in nearly 50% of cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rad07_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rad07-37">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EOP10_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-EOP10-38">[37]</a></sup> Other commonly isolated bacteria include <i><a href="/wiki/Haemophilus_influenzae" title="Haemophilus influenzae">Haemophilus influenzae</a></i> in 20%, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chlamydophila_pneumoniae" title="Chlamydophila pneumoniae">Chlamydophila pneumoniae</a></i> in 13%, and <i><a href="/wiki/Mycoplasma_pneumoniae" title="Mycoplasma pneumoniae">Mycoplasma pneumoniae</a></i> in 3% of cases;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rad07_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rad07-37">[36]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Staphylococcus_aureus" title="Staphylococcus aureus">Staphylococcus aureus</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/Moraxella_catarrhalis" title="Moraxella catarrhalis">Moraxella catarrhalis</a></i>; and <i><a href="/wiki/Legionella_pneumophila" title="Legionella pneumophila">Legionella pneumophila</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBMED05_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED05-22">[21]</a></sup> A number of <a href="/wiki/Drug_resistance" title="Drug resistance">drug-resistant</a> versions of the above infections are becoming more common, including drug-resistant <i>Streptococcus pneumoniae</i> (DRSP) and <a href="/wiki/Methicillin-resistant_Staphylococcus_aureus" title="Methicillin-resistant Staphylococcus aureus">methicillin-resistant <i>Staphylococcus aureus</i></a> (MRSA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>The spreading of organisms is facilitated by certain risk factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBMED05_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED05-22">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">Alcoholism</a> is associated with <i>Streptococcus pneumoniae</i>, <a href="/wiki/Anaerobic_organism" title="Anaerobic organism">anaerobic organisms</a>, and <i>Mycobacterium tuberculosis</i>; smoking facilitates the effects of <i>Streptococcus pneumoniae</i>, <i>Haemophilus influenzae</i>, <i>Moraxella catarrhalis</i>, and <i>Legionella pneumophila</i>. Exposure to birds is associated with <i><a href="/wiki/Chlamydia_psittaci" title="Chlamydia psittaci">Chlamydia psittaci</a></i>; farm animals with <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coxiella_burnetti" title="Coxiella burnetti">Coxiella burnetti</a></i>; aspiration of stomach contents with anaerobic organisms; and <a href="/wiki/Cystic_fibrosis" title="Cystic fibrosis">cystic fibrosis</a> with <i><a href="/wiki/Pseudomonas_aeruginosa" title="Pseudomonas aeruginosa">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</a></i> and <i>Staphylococcus aureus</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBMED05_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED05-22">[21]</a></sup> <i>Streptococcus pneumoniae</i> is more common in the winter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBMED05_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED05-22">[21]</a></sup> and it should be suspected in persons aspirating a large number of anaerobic organisms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-5"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Viruses">Viruses</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Viral_pneumonia" title="Viral pneumonia">Viral pneumonia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SARS_xray.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="543" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/SARS_xray.jpg/220px-SARS_xray.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/SARS_xray.jpg/330px-SARS_xray.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/SARS_xray.jpg/440px-SARS_xray.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SARS_xray.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A chest x-ray of a patient with severe viral pneumonia due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Severe_acute_respiratory_syndrome" title="Severe acute respiratory syndrome">SARS</a></div></div></div>
<p>In adults, viruses account for about one third of pneumonia cases,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-7"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup> and in children for about 15% of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup> Commonly implicated agents include <a href="/wiki/Rhinovirus" title="Rhinovirus">rhinoviruses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus" title="Coronavirus">coronaviruses</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Influenza_virus" title="Influenza virus">influenza virus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_syncytial_virus" title="Respiratory syncytial virus">respiratory syncytial virus</a> (RSV), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adenovirus" title="Adenovirus">adenovirus</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parainfluenza" title="Parainfluenza">parainfluenza</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-8"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viral09_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Viral09-40">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Herpes_simplex_virus" title="Herpes simplex virus">Herpes simplex virus</a> rarely causes pneumonia, except in groups such as newborns, persons with cancer, transplant recipients, and people with significant burns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Text2010_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Text2010-41">[40]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Organ_transplantation" title="Organ transplantation">organ transplantation</a> or in otherwise <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immunocompromised" title="Immunocompromised">immunocompromised</a> persons, there are high rates of <a href="/wiki/Cytomegalovirus" title="Cytomegalovirus">cytomegalovirus</a> pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Text2010_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Text2010-41">[40]</a></sup> Those with viral infections may be secondarily infected with the bacteria <i>Streptococcus pneumoniae</i>, <i>Staphylococcus aureus</i>, or <i>Haemophilus influenzae</i>, particularly when other health problems are present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-6"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup> Different viruses predominate at different times of the year; during <a href="/wiki/Flu_season" title="Flu season">flu season</a>, for example, influenza may account for more than half of all viral cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-3"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup> Outbreaks of other viruses also occur occasionally, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hantaviruses" title="Hantaviruses">hantaviruses</a> and coronaviruses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-4"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Severe_acute_respiratory_syndrome_coronavirus_2" title="Severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2">Severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2</a> (SARS-CoV-2) can also result in pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fungi">Fungi</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fungal_pneumonia" title="Fungal pneumonia">Fungal pneumonia</a></div>
<p>Fungal pneumonia is uncommon, but occurs more commonly in individuals with <a href="/wiki/Immunodeficiency" title="Immunodeficiency">weakened immune systems</a> due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immunosuppressive_drug" title="Immunosuppressive drug">immunosuppressive drugs</a>, or other medical problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBMED05_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED05-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fungus2009_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fungus2009-43">[42]</a></sup> It is most often caused by <i><a href="/wiki/Histoplasmosis" title="Histoplasmosis">Histoplasma capsulatum</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blastomyces" title="Blastomyces">Blastomyces</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cryptococcus_neoformans" title="Cryptococcus neoformans">Cryptococcus neoformans</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pneumocystis_jiroveci" title="Pneumocystis jiroveci">Pneumocystis jiroveci</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Pneumocystis_pneumonia" title="Pneumocystis pneumonia">pneumocystis pneumonia</a>, or PCP), and <i><a href="/wiki/Coccidioides_immitis" title="Coccidioides immitis">Coccidioides immitis</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Histoplasmosis" title="Histoplasmosis">Histoplasmosis</a> is most common in the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_embayment" title="Mississippi embayment">Mississippi River basin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coccidioidomycosis" title="Coccidioidomycosis">coccidioidomycosis</a> is most common in the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwestern United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBMED05_22-7"><a href="#cite_note-EBMED05-22">[21]</a></sup> The number of cases of fungal pneumonia has been increasing in the latter half of the 20th century due to increasing travel and rates of immunosuppression in the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fungus2009_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fungus2009-43">[42]</a></sup> For people infected with <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>, PCP is a common <a href="/wiki/Opportunistic_infection" title="Opportunistic infection">opportunistic infection</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ewa2015_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ewa2015-44">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parasites">Parasites</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parasitic_pneumonia" title="Parasitic pneumonia">Parasitic pneumonia</a></div>
<p>A variety of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">parasites</a> can affect the lungs, including <i><a href="/wiki/Toxoplasma_gondii" title="Toxoplasma gondii">Toxoplasma gondii</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Strongyloides_stercoralis" title="Strongyloides stercoralis">Strongyloides stercoralis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ascaris_lumbricoides" title="Ascaris lumbricoides">Ascaris lumbricoides</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Plasmodium_malariae" title="Plasmodium malariae">Plasmodium malariae</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M37_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-M37-45">[44]</a></sup> These organisms typically enter the body through direct contact with the skin, ingestion, or via an insect vector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M37_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-M37-45">[44]</a></sup> Except for <i><a href="/wiki/Paragonimus_westermani" title="Paragonimus westermani">Paragonimus westermani</a></i>, most parasites do not specifically affect the lungs but involve the lungs secondarily to other sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M37_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-M37-45">[44]</a></sup> Some parasites, in particular those belonging to the <i>Ascaris</i> and <i>Strongyloides</i> genera, stimulate a strong <a href="/wiki/Eosinophilic" title="Eosinophilic">eosinophilic</a> reaction, which may result in <a href="/wiki/Eosinophilic_pneumonia" title="Eosinophilic pneumonia">eosinophilic pneumonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M37_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-M37-45">[44]</a></sup> In other infections, such as malaria, lung involvement is due primarily to <a href="/wiki/Cytokine" title="Cytokine">cytokine</a>-induced <a href="/wiki/Systemic_inflammation" title="Systemic inflammation">systemic inflammation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M37_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-M37-45">[44]</a></sup> In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_world" title="Developed world">developed world</a>, these infections are most common in people returning from travel or in immigrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M37_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-M37-45">[44]</a></sup> Around the world, parasitic pneumonia is most common in the immunodeficient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noninfectious">Noninfectious</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Idiopathic_interstitial_pneumonia" title="Idiopathic interstitial pneumonia">Idiopathic interstitial pneumonia</a></div>
<p>Idiopathic interstitial pneumonia or noninfectious pneumonia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> is a class of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diffuse_lung_disease" title="Diffuse lung disease">diffuse lung diseases</a>. They include <a href="/wiki/Diffuse_alveolar_damage" title="Diffuse alveolar damage">diffuse alveolar damage</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organizing_pneumonia" title="Organizing pneumonia">organizing pneumonia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nonspecific_interstitial_pneumonia" title="Nonspecific interstitial pneumonia">nonspecific interstitial pneumonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lymphocytic_interstitial_pneumonia" title="Lymphocytic interstitial pneumonia">lymphocytic interstitial pneumonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desquamative_interstitial_pneumonia" title="Desquamative interstitial pneumonia">desquamative interstitial pneumonia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_bronchiolitis_interstitial_lung_disease" title="Respiratory bronchiolitis interstitial lung disease">respiratory bronchiolitis interstitial lung disease</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Usual_interstitial_pneumonia" title="Usual interstitial pneumonia">usual interstitial pneumonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lipoid_pneumonia" title="Lipoid pneumonia">Lipoid pneumonia</a> is another rare cause due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lipids" title="Lipids">lipids</a> entering the lung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Had2010_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Had2010-49">[48]</a></sup> These lipids can either be inhaled or spread to the lungs from elsewhere in the body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Had2010_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Had2010-49">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mechanisms">Mechanisms</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Pneumonia_cartoon.jpg"><img alt="A schematic diagram of the human lungs with an empty circle on the left representing a normal alveolus and one on the right showing an alveolus full of fluid as in pneumonia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="611" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="354" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/New_Pneumonia_cartoon.jpg/290px-New_Pneumonia_cartoon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/New_Pneumonia_cartoon.jpg/435px-New_Pneumonia_cartoon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fb/New_Pneumonia_cartoon.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Pneumonia_cartoon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pneumonia fills the lung's <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_alveolus" title="Pulmonary alveolus">alveoli</a> with fluid, hindering oxygenation. The alveolus on the left is normal, whereas the one on the right is full of fluid from pneumonia.</div></div></div>
<p>Pneumonia frequently starts as an <a href="/wiki/Upper_respiratory_tract_infection" title="Upper respiratory tract infection">upper respiratory tract infection</a> that moves into the lower respiratory tract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PedNA09_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-PedNA09-50">[49]</a></sup> It is a type of pneumonitis (lung inflammation).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> The normal flora of the upper airway give protection by competing with pathogens for nutrients. In the lower airways, <a href="/wiki/Cough_reflex" title="Cough reflex">reflexes of the glottis</a>, actions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Complement_protein" title="Complement protein">complement proteins</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immunoglobulin" title="Immunoglobulin">immunoglobulins</a> are important for protection. Micro<a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_aspiration" title="Pulmonary aspiration">aspiration</a> of contaminated secretions can infect the lower airways and cause pneumonia. The progress of pneumonia is determined by the virulence of the organism; the amount of organism required to start an infection; and the body's immune response against the infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elena_2015_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elena_2015-36">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bacterial">Bacterial</span></h3>
<p>Most bacteria enter the lungs via small <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_aspiration" title="Pulmonary aspiration">aspirations</a> of organisms residing in the throat or nose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-7"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> Half of normal people have these small aspirations during sleep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M32_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-M32-29">[28]</a></sup> While the throat always contains bacteria, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virulent" title="Virulent">potentially infectious</a> ones reside there only at certain times and under certain conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M32_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-M32-29">[28]</a></sup> A minority of types of bacteria such as <i><a href="/wiki/Mycobacterium_tuberculosis" title="Mycobacterium tuberculosis">Mycobacterium tuberculosis</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Legionella_pneumophila" title="Legionella pneumophila">Legionella pneumophila</a></i> reach the lungs via contaminated airborne droplets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-8"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> Bacteria can also spread via the blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOPrevent2012_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-WHOPrevent2012-26">[25]</a></sup> Once in the lungs, bacteria may invade the spaces between cells and between alveoli, where the <a href="/wiki/Macrophage" title="Macrophage">macrophages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neutrophil" title="Neutrophil">neutrophils</a> (defensive <a href="/wiki/White_blood_cell" title="White blood cell">white blood cells</a>) attempt to inactivate the bacteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> The neutrophils also release <a href="/wiki/Cytokine" title="Cytokine">cytokines</a>, causing a general activation of the immune system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fein2006_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fein2006-53">[52]</a></sup> This leads to the fever, chills, and fatigue common in bacterial pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fein2006_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fein2006-53">[52]</a></sup> The neutrophils, bacteria, and fluid from surrounding blood vessels fill the alveoli, resulting in the consolidation seen on chest X-ray.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Viral">Viral</span></h3>
<p>Viruses may reach the lung by a number of different routes. Respiratory syncytial virus is typically contracted when people touch contaminated objects and then touch their eyes or nose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-5"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup> Other viral infections occur when contaminated airborne droplets are inhaled through the nose or mouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-9"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> Once in the upper airway, the viruses may make their way into the lungs, where they invade the cells lining the airways, alveoli, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lung_parenchyma" title="Lung parenchyma">lung parenchyma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-6"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup> Some viruses such as measles and herpes simplex may reach the lungs via the blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gary2010_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gary2010-55">[54]</a></sup> The invasion of the lungs may lead to varying degrees of cell death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-7"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup> When the immune system responds to the infection, even more lung damage may occur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31_39-8"><a href="#cite_note-M31-39">[38]</a></sup> Primarily <a href="/wiki/White_blood_cell" title="White blood cell">white blood cells</a>, mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mononuclear_cell" title="Mononuclear cell">mononuclear cells</a>, generate the inflammation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gary2010_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gary2010-55">[54]</a></sup> As well as damaging the lungs, many viruses simultaneously affect other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" title="Organ (anatomy)">organs</a> and thus disrupt other body functions. Viruses also make the body more susceptible to bacterial infections; in this way, bacterial pneumonia can occur at the same time as viral pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viral09_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Viral09-40">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis">Diagnosis</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097025294">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096940132">.mw-parser-output .listen .side-box-text{line-height:1.1em}.mw-parser-output .listen-plain{border:none;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded{width:100%;margin:0;border-width:1px 0 0 0;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-header{padding:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded .listen-header{padding:2px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen-file-header{padding:4px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen .description{padding-top:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen .mw-tmh-player{max-width:100%}@media(max-width:719px){.mw-parser-output .listen{clear:both}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .listen:not(.listen-noimage){width:320px}.mw-parser-output .listen-left{overflow:visible;float:left}.mw-parser-output .listen-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint">
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:Crackles_pneumoniaO.ogg" title="File:Crackles pneumoniaO.ogg">Crackles</a></div>
<div><audio controls="" data-durationhint="14" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Crackles_pneumoniaO.ogg" id="mwe_player_3" preload="none" style="width:232px;" width="232"><source data-bandwidth="46439" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (46 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c7/Crackles_pneumoniaO.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="89200" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/c7/Crackles_pneumoniaO.ogg/Crackles_pneumoniaO.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/><track data-dir="ltr" kind="subtitles" label="English ‪(en)‬" src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3ACrackles_pneumoniaO.ogg&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" srclang="en" type="text/vtt"/></audio></div>
<div class="description">Crackles heard in the lungs of a person with pneumonia using a stethoscope.</div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr/><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<p>Pneumonia is typically diagnosed based on a combination of physical signs and often a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest_X-ray" title="Chest X-ray">chest X-ray</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diag10_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Diag10-56">[55]</a></sup> In adults with normal vital signs and a normal lung examination, the diagnosis is unlikely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> However, the underlying cause can be difficult to confirm, as there is no definitive test able to distinguish between bacterial and non-bacterial cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_12-9"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diag10_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Diag10-56">[55]</a></sup> The overall impression of a physician appears to be at least as good as decision rules for making or excluding the diagnosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis_in_children">Diagnosis in children</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> has defined pneumonia in children clinically based on either a <a href="/wiki/Cough" title="Cough">cough</a> or difficulty breathing and a rapid respiratory rate, chest indrawing, or a decreased level of consciousness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOBook_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHOBook-59">[58]</a></sup> A rapid respiratory rate is defined as greater than 60 breaths per minute in children under 2 months old, greater than 50 breaths per minute in children 2 months to 1 year old, or greater than 40 breaths per minute in children 1 to 5 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOBook_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHOBook-59">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>In children, low oxygen levels and lower chest indrawing are more <a href="/wiki/Sensitivity_and_specificity" title="Sensitivity and specificity">sensitive</a> than hearing chest <a href="/wiki/Crackles" title="Crackles">crackles</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Stethoscope" title="Stethoscope">stethoscope</a> or increased respiratory rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Grunting and nasal flaring may be other useful signs in children less than five years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lack of wheezing is an indicator of <i><a href="/wiki/Mycoplasma_pneumoniae" title="Mycoplasma pneumoniae">Mycoplasma pneumoniae</a></i> in children with pneumonia, but as an indicator it is not accurate enough to decide whether or not <a href="/wiki/Macrolide" title="Macrolide">macrolide</a> treatment should be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang2012_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2012-62">[61]</a></sup> The presence of chest pain in children with pneumonia doubles the probability of <i>Mycoplasma pneumoniae</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang2012_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2012-62">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis_in_adults">Diagnosis in adults</span></h3>
<p>In general, in adults, investigations are not needed in mild cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BTS09_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-BTS09-63">[62]</a></sup> There is a very low risk of pneumonia if all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vital_sign" title="Vital sign">vital signs</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest_auscultation" title="Chest auscultation">auscultation</a> are normal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/C-reactive_protein" title="C-reactive protein">C-reactive protein</a> (CRP) may help support the diagnosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> For those with CRP less than 20 mg/L without convincing evidence of pneumonia, antibiotics are not recommended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elena_2015_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Elena_2015-36">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Procalcitonin" title="Procalcitonin">Procalcitonin</a> may help determine the cause and support decisions about who should receive antibiotics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid29037960_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid29037960-66">[65]</a></sup> Antibiotics are encouraged if the procalcitonin level reaches 0.25 μg/L, strongly encouraged if it reaches 0.5 μg/L, and strongly discouraged if the level is below 0.10 μg/L.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elena_2015_36-3"><a href="#cite_note-Elena_2015-36">[35]</a></sup> In people requiring hospitalization, <a href="/wiki/Pulse_oximetry" title="Pulse oximetry">pulse oximetry</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest_radiography" title="Chest radiography">chest radiography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blood_test" title="Blood test">blood tests</a> – including a <a href="/wiki/Complete_blood_count" title="Complete blood count">complete blood count</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serum_electrolytes" title="Serum electrolytes">serum electrolytes</a>, C-reactive protein level, and possibly <a href="/wiki/Liver_function_tests" title="Liver function tests">liver function tests</a> – are recommended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BTS09_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-BTS09-63">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>The diagnosis of <a href="/wiki/Influenza-like_illness" title="Influenza-like illness">influenza-like illness</a> can be made based on the signs and symptoms; however, confirmation of an influenza infection requires testing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ILI05_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-ILI05-67">[66]</a></sup> Thus, treatment is frequently based on the presence of influenza in the community or a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_influenza_diagnostic_test" title="Rapid influenza diagnostic test">rapid influenza test</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ILI05_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-ILI05-67">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_exam">Physical exam</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Physical_examination" title="Physical examination">Physical examination</a> may sometimes reveal <a href="/wiki/Hypotension" title="Hypotension">low blood pressure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tachycardia" title="Tachycardia">high heart rate</a>, or low <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxygenation_(medical)" title="Oxygenation (medical)">oxygen saturation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-10"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> The respiratory rate may be faster than normal, and this may occur a day or two before other signs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-11"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M32_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-M32-29">[28]</a></sup> Examination of the chest may be normal, but it may show decreased expansion on the affected side. Harsh breath sounds from the larger airways that are transmitted through the inflamed lung are termed <a href="/wiki/Bronchus" title="Bronchus">bronchial</a> breathing and are heard on auscultation with a <a href="/wiki/Stethoscope" title="Stethoscope">stethoscope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-12"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crackles" title="Crackles">Crackles</a> (rales) may be heard over the affected area during <a href="/wiki/Inhalation" title="Inhalation">inspiration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-13"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Percussion_(medicine)" title="Percussion (medicine)">Percussion</a> may be dulled over the affected lung, and increased, rather than decreased, <a href="/wiki/Vocal_resonation" title="Vocal resonation">vocal resonance</a> distinguishes pneumonia from a <a href="/wiki/Pleural_effusion" title="Pleural effusion">pleural effusion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMJ06_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-BMJ06-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imaging">Imaging</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:X-ray_of_lobar_pneumonia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2407" data-file-width="3027" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/X-ray_of_lobar_pneumonia.jpg/220px-X-ray_of_lobar_pneumonia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/X-ray_of_lobar_pneumonia.jpg/330px-X-ray_of_lobar_pneumonia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/X-ray_of_lobar_pneumonia.jpg/440px-X-ray_of_lobar_pneumonia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:X-ray_of_lobar_pneumonia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A chest X-ray showing a very prominent wedge-shaped area of airspace consolidation in the right lung characteristic of acute bacterial lobar pneumonia</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CT_scan_of_the_chest,_demonstrating_right-sided_pneumonia.jpg"><img alt="A black-and-white image shows the internal organs in cross-section as generated by CT. Where one would expect black on the left, one sees a whiter area with black sticks through it." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2140" data-file-width="3006" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/CT_scan_of_the_chest%2C_demonstrating_right-sided_pneumonia.jpg/220px-CT_scan_of_the_chest%2C_demonstrating_right-sided_pneumonia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/CT_scan_of_the_chest%2C_demonstrating_right-sided_pneumonia.jpg/330px-CT_scan_of_the_chest%2C_demonstrating_right-sided_pneumonia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/CT_scan_of_the_chest%2C_demonstrating_right-sided_pneumonia.jpg/440px-CT_scan_of_the_chest%2C_demonstrating_right-sided_pneumonia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CT_scan_of_the_chest,_demonstrating_right-sided_pneumonia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>CT of the chest demonstrating right-sided pneumonia (left side of the image)</div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Chest_radiograph" title="Chest radiograph">chest radiograph</a> is frequently used in diagnosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Develop11_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-Develop11-24">[23]</a></sup> In people with mild disease, imaging is needed only in those with potential complications, those not having improved with treatment, or those in which the cause is uncertain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Develop11_24-4"><a href="#cite_note-Develop11-24">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BTS09_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-BTS09-63">[62]</a></sup> If a person is sufficiently sick to require hospitalization, a chest radiograph is recommended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BTS09_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-BTS09-63">[62]</a></sup> Findings do not always match the severity of disease and do not reliably separate between bacterial and viral infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Develop11_24-5"><a href="#cite_note-Develop11-24">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>X-ray presentations of pneumonia may be classified as <a href="/wiki/Lobar_pneumonia" title="Lobar pneumonia">lobar pneumonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bronchopneumonia" title="Bronchopneumonia">bronchopneumonia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lobular_pneumonia" title="Lobular pneumonia">lobular pneumonia</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstitial_pneumonia" title="Interstitial pneumonia">interstitial pneumonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Bacterial, community-acquired pneumonia classically show <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lung_consolidation" title="Lung consolidation">lung consolidation</a> of one <a href="/wiki/Bronchopulmonary_segment" title="Bronchopulmonary segment">lung segmental lobe</a>, which is known as lobar pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rad07_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rad07-37">[36]</a></sup> However, findings may vary, and other patterns are common in other types of pneumonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rad07_37-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rad07-37">[36]</a></sup> Aspiration pneumonia may present with bilateral opacities primarily in the bases of the lungs and on the right side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rad07_37-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rad07-37">[36]</a></sup> Radiographs of viral pneumonia may appear normal, appear hyper-inflated, have bilateral patchy areas, or present similar to bacterial pneumonia with lobar consolidation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rad07_37-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rad07-37">[36]</a></sup> Radiologic findings may not be present in the early stages of the disease, especially in the presence of dehydration, or may be difficult to interpret in the <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obese</a> or those with a history of lung disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinic2011_25-14"><a href="#cite_note-Clinic2011-25">[24]</a></sup> Complications such as <a href="/wiki/Pleural_effusion" title="Pleural effusion">pleural effusion</a> may also be found on chest radiographs. Laterolateral chest radiographs can increase the diagnostic accuracy of lung consolidation and pleural effusion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elena_2015_36-4"><a href="#cite_note-Elena_2015-36">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/CT_scan" title="CT scan">CT scan</a> can give additional information in indeterminate cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rad07_37-6"><a href="#cite_note-Rad07-37">[36]</a></sup> CT scans can also provide more details in those with an unclear chest radiograph (for example <a href="/wiki/Occult" title="Occult">occult</a> pneumonia in <a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">chronic obstructive pulmonary disease</a>) and can exclude <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_embolism" title="Pulmonary embolism">pulmonary embolism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fungal_pneumonia" title="Fungal pneumonia">fungal pneumonia</a> and detect <a href="/wiki/Lung_abscess" title="Lung abscess">lung abscess</a> in those who are not responding to treatments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elena_2015_36-5"><a href="#cite_note-Elena_2015-36">[35]</a></sup> However, CT scans are more expensive, have a higher dose of radiation, and cannot be done at bedside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elena_2015_36-6"><a href="#cite_note-Elena_2015-36">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lung_ultrasound" title="Lung ultrasound">Lung ultrasound</a> may also be useful in helping to make the diagnosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> Ultrasound is radiation free and can be done at bedside. However, ultrasound requires specific skills to operate the machine and interpret the findings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elena_2015_36-7"><a href="#cite_note-Elena_2015-36">[35]</a></sup> It may be more accurate than chest X-ray.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
